/>\r\n<br />\r\n<!--field ( Notice Type )-->\r\n<p>NCI is fulfilling the&nbsp;Department of the Air Force, Air Materiel Command, Electronic System Center (ESC), requirement for Reliability and Maintainability Information System (REMIS) Subject Matter Experts (SMEs).</p>\r\n<p><strong>BACKGROUND:</strong></p>\r\n<p>REMIS is a large, complex legacy information system featuring a centralized database containing Air Force-wide inventory/status/utilization data, maintenance data and configuration data. The data is reported from base level units and operating locations all over the world. Sustainment of REMIS includes all activities required to keep the system hardware, software and database useable 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. <br />\r\n<br />\r\nREMIS was designed to enhance the front-end design of new weapon systems and to increase the readiness and sustainability of existing United States Air Force weapon systems by improving the availability, accuracy and flow of essential equipment information. REMIS provides the capability to collect, edit, validate, process, store and report reliability and maintainability data on Aerospace Vehicles, Trainers, Automated Test Equipment (ATE), selected Support Equipment (SE) and Communications-Electronics (C-E) equipment in the following functional areas: Equipment Maintenance, Time Compliance Technical Order (TCTO), Time Change Inspection (TCI), Configuration, Debriefing, Inventory, Status and Utilization. REMIS functionality is split across its subsystems <br />\r\n<br />\r\n<br />\r\n<strong>REQUIREMENTS:</strong></p>\r\n<p>The REMIS PMO requires functional and technical SME support. </p>\r\n<p>SMEs are individuals with a specific level of expertise in certain key system areas or disciplines and are knowledgeable about the domain being represented. This professional provides unique and/or in-depth functional and technical knowledge on the application and system operations. REMIS SMEs are required to have expert knowledge of REMIS and its environment, the Air Force users and processes that support, perform and manage weapons systems maintenance for the Air Force enterprise, and the Air Force directives that document those Air Force maintenance processes (AFI 16-402, AFI 21-103, AFI 21-101, and the 00-20 series Technical Orders). REMIS SMEs have in depth understanding of REMIS functionality and the importance of that functionality to formation of policy and weapon system decision making</p>\r\n<p>The scope of the SMEs responsibilities include: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Translating user requirements into system specifications, data management plans, configuration management plans, life cycle management documentation, integrated logistics support plans and related operational summaries </li>\r\n    <li>Gathering information from users, defining work problems and designing a system and assorted procedures to resolve problems </li>\r\n    <li>Assisting in the design, development, analysis, test and maintenance of logical and physical databases in order to meet functional requirements </li>\r\n    <li>Writing specification manuals and user documentation for client or user personnel </li>\r\n    <li>Directing enterprise wide (world-wide) strategic systems planning, business information planning, business and analysis </li>\r\n    <li>Managing functional, process, and data modeling in support of the planning and analysis efforts </li>\r\n    <li>Examining and analyzing current and contemplated operations for developing, defining, and coordinating user requirements which will satisfy the total program need </li>\r\n    <li>Reviewing data design, proposed system revisions, and test results to ensure functional requirements are met </li>\r\n    <li>Evaluate proposed system and software change and corrective request actions. System and software changes are documented as Advance Change Study Notices (ACSNs), Engineering Change Proposals (ECPs), Contract Change Proposals (CCPs), Information Technology/National Security System Requirements Document (ITSRDs) (approved by a higher headquarters) and Requests for Deviation and Waiver. System corrective actions are documented as REMIS Automated Problem Reports (RAPRs) </li>\r\n    <li>Analyze reported software problems, determine the severity of the problems and recommend priorities and solutions for consideration by the subsystem lead </li>\r\n    <li>Provide REMIS end-user support at the system and subsystem levels and below </li>\r\n    <li>Provide support at the subsystem level through active participation in Technical Interchange Meetings (TIMs), Test Plan Working Groups (TPWGs), Interface Control Working Groups (ICWGs) and Discrepancy Review Boards (DRBs) </li>\r\n    <li>Participate in system reviews, design &ldquo;walk-throughs,&rdquo; and ad hoc PMO teams established to perform tests and review test results of software enhancements/fixes </li>\r\n    <li>Be a member of a REMIS functional and technical team providing REMIS system expertise to various other identified development teams. This includes, but may not be limited to, the Integrated Maintenance Data System (IMDS, formerly known as the Core Automated Maintenance System (CAMS)), the Global Combat Support System-Air (GCSS-AF) Data Services, Nuclear Weapons Related Material Positive Inventory Control (NWRM/PIC) and the Expeditionary Combat Support System (ECSS) </li>\r\n    <li>Participate in activities related to the migration of REMIS into the GCSS-AF platform/system. Participation may include, but not be limited to, attending meetings, leading discussions or working groups and assisting with the production of various documents. </li>\r\n    <li>Act as the REMIS focal point for REMIS user connectivity and Air Force Primary Key Infrastructure (PKI) requirements. Activities shall include, but may not be limited to, receiving/tracking user connectivity requests, facilitating the accomplishment of requests, assisting users with day-to-day connectivity issues and evaluating/recommending revisions to user-oriented documentation pertaining to REMIS connectivity </li>\r\n    <li>Act as the REMIS focal point for Federal Desktop Core Configuration (FDCC). Activities shall include, but may not be limited to, reviewing and evaluating FDCC releases and reporting status and compliancy </li>\r\n    <li>Serve as the REMISTALK application system administrator and customer service representative. REMISTALK is the ad hoc query capability of REMIS. Activities shall include, but may not be limited to, evaluating and testing REMISTALK capabilities, developing new REMISTALK views and expanding or modify existing views and troubleshooting/testing to improve the capabilities of current REMISTALK views to comply with user requirements and/or expanding REMIS capabilities. The contractor shall provide direct customer support by creating, modifying and troubleshooting REMISTALK views, algorithms and FOCUS&trade; software applications. Additionally, the contractor shall extract REMIS data for government agencies and contractors who require the data, but may not have REMIS access. Historically, this support has consisted of approximately fifteen (15) to thirty (30) special assistance requests per month. Finally, the contractor shall act as the REMISTALK focal point for, and assist in supporting, GCSS-AF Data Services. Support may include, but not be limited to, becoming familiar with and assisting in GCSS-AF Data Services data retrieval, identifying related issues, attending REMIS/GCSS-AF Data Services meetings and providing other support as needed. </li>\r\n    <li>Accomplish monitoring and surveillance of the approximately twenty five (25) System-to-System Input (SSI)/System-to-System Output (SSO) interfaces. only organization wholly dedicated to leading the discovery, development, and integration of warfighting technologies for&nbsp;America's air, space and cyberspace forces. <br />\r\n<br />\r\nAFRL traces its roots back to the vision of early airpower leaders who understood science as the key to air supremacy. The passionate commitment of&nbsp;AFRL's people to realize this vision has helped create the world's best air, space and cyberspace force. </p>\r\n<p><strong>REQUIREMENTS:</strong><br />\r\n<br />\r\nCall 1: </p>\r\n<p>The Department of Defense is requesting proposals which extend the state of the art in modeling and simulation as it is applied during the systems acquisition process. This includes, but is not limited to: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Integration of design models with analysis tools </li>\r\n    <li>Identification of critical design features based on technology and manufacturing maturity, cost, quality, reliability or schedule risk </li>\r\n    <li>Visualization of assembly operations at multiple levels of detail </li>\r\n    <li>Integration of high fidelity cost models at all levels of design and system integration </li>\r\n    <li>Prediction and analysis of supply chain risks </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>Call 2: </p>\r\n<p>The objective of this program is to eliminate the use of leaded solder in the manufacture, assembly of electronic systems and to demonstrate applicable repair and rework techniques to support the sustainment portion of the system life cycle. White papers are therefore being sought that address: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Maturation of the manufacturing capability(ies) which fabricates the subsystem components </li>\r\n    <li>Ability to use existing ECAD tools for system design </li>\r\n    <li>Scale up of innovative materials and manufacturing processes that can be readily incorporated into a production facility possibly supporting field level repair </li>\r\n    <li>Lead free manufacturing technology issues including but not limited to:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Modular and flexible design concepts </li>\r\n        <li>Low cost tooling concepts </li>\r\n        <li>Process controls and inspection methods for components and completed subsystems </li>\r\n        <li>Repair and rework and test concepts </li>\r\n        <li>Reduced footprint manufacturing systems </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>Call 3:</p>\r\n<p>The aim of this program will be to dramatically reduce the overall cycle and turnaround times in order to reduce both costs and lead times for airframes for fixed and/or rotary wing aircraft. White papers are sought for any of the following areas: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Achieve dramatic reductions in nonrecurring fabrication and assembly tooling (jig) costs, numbers, and lead time through technologies such as:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Out of autoclave composite materials </li>\r\n        <li>Use of the structure as the assembly jig </li>\r\n        <li>Direct digital manufacturing of polymer and metallic components </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Widespread application of unitized structures for composite and metallic aircraft:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Bonded structures </li>\r\n        <li>Friction stir welding </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Innovative approaches reducing capital requirements for drilling and milling for structural assembly:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Unitized structures </li>\r\n        <li>Adaptive (intelligent) machining including advancements in measurement and position location </li>\r\n        <li>Improved accuracy of industrial robotic drilling </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>Call 4:</p>\r\n<p>The objective of this program is to dramatically reduce the manufacturing cost and lead times of CLAS by identifying and refining the requisite manufacturing technologies required for future manned and unmanned platforms. There are significantly different manufacturing processes and parts count associated with composites that are not currently addressed with the procurement and life cycle management processes. Composite structures, when compared to metallic structure, are perceived to imply more risk than the associated cost advantages due to insufficient characterization of the life cycle benefits from optimal composite use </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Producibility Analysis\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Develop and demonstrate capability to assess producibility of designs at all stages of development. White papers should illustrate where closed expression scores of producibility or integration with real-time shop floor information can be used to avoid costly downstream manufacturing problems. <br />\r\n        </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Preservation and Manufacturing of Legacy Components<strong>:&nbsp;</strong>\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Enable legacy components to be compatible with product lifecycle management processes.&nbsp;Demonstrate the ability to create 3D CAD models where drawings are incomplete or do not exist &ndash; i.e. reverse engineering &ndash; and enable CAD based repair or remanufacturing </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Tool Integration:&nbsp;\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Define and address outstanding issues of integration of design models with analysis tools, mechanical and electronic designs, or other integration challenges encountered during detailed design </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Visualization Environments:&nbsp;\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Develop and demonstrate 3D immersive environments that enable real-time visualization of design collaboration.&nbsp;Develop and demonstrate innovative ways to effectively portray trade space data to support accurate decision making and Analysis of Alternatives, including supply base status and relevant cost information </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Supply chain Simulation and War Gaming:&nbsp;\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Pilot demonstrations of extensive, distributed supply chain simulations that allow the acquiring or sustaining organization to perform Monte Carlo analysis of supply base vulnerabilities </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>Call #6:</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Rapid Manufacturing is a new area of manufacturing developed from a family of technologies known as Rapid Prototyping. Rapid Prototyping typically utilizes advanced layer manufacturing technologies that can quickly generate complex three-dimensional objects directly from computer-based models devised by Computer Aided Design (CAD). This computer representation is sliced into two-dimensional layers, whose descriptions are sent to the fabrication equipment to build the part layer by layer. Rapid prototyping includes many different fabrication technologies. Stereolithography (SL), selective laser sintering (SLS), laminated object manufacturing (LOM), and fused deposition modeling (FDM) are a few examples. These Rapid Prototyping processes have already had the effect of both improving products and reducing their development time. Rapid Manufacturing is an attempt to transition these prototyping techniques to the manufacturing floor. This form of manufacturing can be incredibly cost-effective and the process is far more flexible than conventional manufacturing. Rapid Prototyping processes have been shown to be economically feasible for use in the manufacture of non structural parts in quantities. This Rapid Manufacturing effort will focus on the use of these Rapid Prototyping processes in the fabrication and/or assembly of Aerospace Structures </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>White papers are therefore being sought that address:&nbsp;</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Identification and demonstration of the use of rapid manufacturing in the fabrication and/or assembly of aerospace structures. Examples of parts that could be fabricated include but are not limited to control surfaces, edges, and ducting. The demonstration articles shall validate the ability of rapid manufacturing techniques to fabricate timely affordable structural components. Emphasis on affordability should concentrate not only on the ability to fabricate components but on the ability of rapid manufacturing to assist in the assembly of components. The contractor shall work with the aerospace OEMs to identify the structural requirements and to establish baseline costs for these structural components and their assembly </li>\r\n    <li>Identification of current, planned or proposed weapon systems which would benefit from the identified RMAS cost reduction techniques/technologies with anticipated cost savings and/or capability improvements </li>\r\n    <li>Manufacturing Readiness Levels (MRLs) shall be used throughout the program as a tool to indicate the level of manufacturing maturity during program execution. The Manufacturing Readiness objective for this program is Level 4-5. A Manufacturing Readiness Assessment (MRA) will be conducted within six months of contract award to baseline the program. The assessment will determine and justify the initial MRL and provide a plan to reach MRL -45. Command, Air Force Research Library, Sensors Directorate, Avionics Vulnerability Mitigation Branch (AFRL/RYWA) has a requirement for research&nbsp;into avionics systems vulnerabilities.</p>\n\n<h4>BACKGROUND</h4>\n\n<p>&nbsp;AFRL/RYW has a need to investigate and develop methodologies, tools, techniques, and capabilities to identify susceptibilities and mitigate vulnerabilities in avionics systems, protect those systems against cyber attack, provide simulation capabilities required to develop, mature and transition advanced sensor and avionics technologies, develop platform architecture technologies that enable revolutionary and agile capabilities, and expand emerging open system architecture standards and approaches for existing and next-generation Air Force and DoD weapon systems in multi-domain environments. The goal is to explore new and emerging concepts related to development, integration, assessment, evaluation, and demonstration of cyber security, open system architecture (OSA), novel avionics and sensor technologies, and multi-domain technologies. For this solicitation, avionics is defined to include manned, unmanned, autonomous, and remotely piloted vehicles, on-board Intelligence, Surveillance, and Reconnaissance (ISR) systems, Electronic Warfare (EW) systems, munitions, and any equipment, component, or subsystem that could compromise mission assurance of the Air Force weapon system or tactical platform.</p>\n\n<h4>REQUIREMENTS</h4>\n\n<p>The TEMPEST program will investigate, develop, mature, prototype and demonstrate methodologies, tools, techniques, and capabilities to identify susceptibilities and mitigate vulnerabilities in avionics systems, protect those systems against cyber-attack, provide simulation capabilities required to develop, mature and transition advanced avionics and sensor technologies, develop platform architecture technologies that enable revolutionary and agile capabilities, and expand emerging open system architecture (OSA) standards and approaches for existing and next-generation Air Force and Department of Defense (DoD) weapon systems in multi-domain environments.</p>\n\n<p>Calls issued against this ARA will:&nbsp;</p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>Develop experimental programs that prototype, integrate and demonstrate promising cyber security and cognitive avionics technologies to increase our platforms&rsquo; and weapon systems&rsquo; survivability and resiliency in the face of multidomain threats and attacks.</li>\n\t<li>Develop, experiment, prototype and integrate, in a laboratory environment, new cognitive, cyber hardened and high speed, flexible system architectures.</li>\n\t<li>Cooperate across the Air Force, DoD, and the Intelligence Community, to develop experimental programs that integrate advanced cyber security and cognitive sensor technologies, techniques, systems and developmental algorithms, new cyber hardened and high speed, flexible system architectures, and advanced avionics, sensors, processing, and exploitation capabilities focused on Command, Control, Communications, Computers, Intelligence, Surveillance and Reconnaissance (C4ISR) onto various weapon systems to create revolutionary capabilities.</li>\n\t<li>Develop experimental programs that implement OSA-based reference&nbsp;architectures to demonstrate the cost and time benefits of applying OSA techniques and align multiple open architecture (OA) standards to prove the interoperability of various standards. Apply and demonstrate tools, technologies, and techniques to more rapidly document, model, simulate, and analyze new OSA-based system capabilities to determine the benefits for individual platforms and the warfighter.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>Calls to be issued against the TEMPEST ARA must a) fall under at least one of the Technical Areas of Interest below:</p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>Technical Areas of Interest:\n\t<ul>\n\t\t<li><strong>Technologies for Assessing Platform Cyber Security: </strong>Focuses on the design and development of technologies that provide tools to test and experimentation (T&amp;E) units and Cyber units (such as Mission Defense Teams or Red Teams) to assess cyber vulnerabilities in weapon systems with embedded computers.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Technologies for Cyber-Hardened Platforms:</strong> Focuses on the design and development of technologies that reduce weapon system vulnerability to cyber-attack.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Technologies for Cyber-Resilient Platforms:</strong> Focuses on the design and development of technologies that counter both known and unknown attack vectors that occur during mission operations to maintain mission capability in cyber contested environments.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Agile System Architecture Development and Integration:</strong> Focuses on the design/procurement, development and demonstration of tools, technologies, and advanced component prototypes to enable affordable, rapid development and integration of new and emerging warfighting capability. Characteristics of these systems include, but are not limited to: capable of performing multiple functions (e.g., radar, communications, and electronic warfare), capable of fusing different types of data collections (i.e., multiple intelligence (multi-INT)), inherently cyber secure and/or resilient to cyber-attack, and compliant with open system architecture standards and approaches.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Open System Architectures for Trusted and Agile Platforms:</strong> Focuses on investigation, through analysis, demonstration and advanced component prototyping, the viability and relevance of current and emerging open system architecture standards and approaches to enable new capability for cyber trusted and agile platforms. This technology area seeks to determine the viability of an OSA implementation prior to system design and development. This technical area shall identify technological advances in open system architecture standards, software, processing, and hardware to demonstrate the viability of modular open system architectures.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Technologies for Modeling &amp; Simulation:</strong> Focuses on the discovery, design and implementation of novel technologies to advance the state-of-the-art in modeling/simulation to faithfully represent transmitters, receivers, electronic systems, hostile and friendly radars, and radio frequency propagation algorithms for use with advanced models and simulations.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Technologies to Advance RF Simulation:</strong> Focuses on defining simulation requirements for accurately demonstrating and evaluating sensor technologies. This technology area includes the design and implementation of prototype hardware (commercial or custom) and corresponding operating software tools to conduct demonstrations of radio frequency receiving or transmitting systems.</li>\n\t\t<li><strong>Techniques, methods and technologies for measuring sensor system performance:</strong> Focuses on developing simulation techniques and methods to rapidly evolve and evaluate advanced sensors and electronic warfare (EW) technologies demonstrated in laboratory environments. Work under this technical area of interest will develop and employ M&amp;S methods to specify requirements, define architectures, conduct design trades, and report assessment and demonstration results.</li>\n\t</ul>\n\t</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p><strong>Call #1: Technologies for Advanced RF Simulation (TARFS) for the IDAL Cognitive Enabling Technologies (ICET)</strong></p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>To develop, implement, and use simulation capabilities required to conduct Integrated Demonstrations and Applications Laboratory (IDAL) multi-spectral synthetic battlespace simulations. Accomplishing this goal requires research into areas such as digital models, man/hardware-in-the-loop simulators, sensor testbeds, simulation capability integration and verification/validation of IDAL RF battlespace simulation integrated capabilities. Recent advances in simulation technologies include increased instantaneous bandwidth, improved waveform fidelity, and expanded dynamic range. Laboratory evaluations of new radar frequency (RF) sensors drive the incorporation of these on-going advances into battlespace simulators. The IDAL synthetic battlespace simulation and generation capabilities will be used to conduct sensor technology applications research in order to transition sensors, information processing and simulation technologies to meet warfighter requirements. This task integrates technology by conducting advanced technology demonstrations and system level evaluations. The efforts supported by this task involve time critical milestones and complex leading-edge technologies for Department of Defense (DoD) weapon system and Foreign Military Sales (FMS) programs</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p><strong>Call #2:&nbsp;Resilient and Agile Mission Systems (RAMS)</strong></p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>Resilient and Agile Mission Systems (RAMS) program leverages current advances in open system architecture standards and approaches, commercial high-speed networking technologies, heterogeneous processing, precision timing, cybersecurity and cyber-resiliency, and advanced computing paradigms such as cloud infrastructure to enable advanced mission system capability. This effort seeks to build upon ongoing research and development in order to prototype a Resilient and Agile Mission Systems architecture for advanced, next-generation avionics. The effort will also continue Open Architecture (OA) improvements such as Open Mission Systems and Unified Command and Control Interface (UCI), as well as, this effort will leverage technological advances such as Cloud Computing, commercial sector technologies such as networking and processing, databases/data storage, data transfers, and open standards/format/protocols. The resulting prototype will provide the platform infrastructure necessary to empower new mission system capability at the speed of relevance to meet the needs of next-generation avionics platforms.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p><strong>Call #3: Agile and Resilient Platform Architectures (ARPA) </strong></p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>The objective of the ARPA program is to perform enhanced development, advanced technology demonstrations, component development and prototyping of tools, techniques, and capabilities to: 1) Identify and mitigate vulnerabilities in avionics systems; 2) Harden and protect avionics systems against cyber-attack; 3) Advance current techniques to detect, respond, and adapt to novel cyber-attacks on avionics in real-time; 4) Demonstrate integrated mission systems and advanced prototype components leveraging current and emerging open system architecture standards and approaches; and 5) Prototype agile, next-generation platform and system of systems architectures to enable rapid integration and fielding of enhanced mission system capability.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p><strong>Call #4:&nbsp;Mission Systems Open Architecture Prototyping, Experimentation, and Demonstration (MOAPED)</strong></p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>To develop and demonstrate technology and advanced component prototype solutions to evolve and expand emerging open architecture (OA) standards and approaches for current and next-generation Air Force and DoD weapon systems. This effort seeks to identify and reduce barriers to adoption as well as demonstrate and prototype tools, technologies, and prototype solutions to enhance OA standards. As a result of the MOAPED effort, mature, robust open architecture solutions will be provided to rapidly integrate mission systems, facilitate mission system capability evolution, as well as sustained competition across the system life-cycle</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p><strong>Call #5:&nbsp;Radio Frequency (RF) Electronic Warfare (EW) Focused Laboratory Evaluations of Critical Technologies (REFLECT)</strong></p>\n\n<ul>\n\t<li>AFRL/RYW has a need to investigate and develop methodologies, tools, techniques, and capabilities to identify susceptibilities and mitigate vulnerabilities in avionics systems, protect those systems against cyber-attack, provide simulation capabilities required to develop, mature and transition advanced sensor and avionics technologies, develop platform architecture technologies that enable revolutionary and agile capabilities, and expand emerging open system architecture standards and approaches for existing and next-generation Air Force and DoD weapon systems in multi-domain environments. The goal is to explore new and emerging concepts related to development, integration, assessment, evaluation, and demonstration of cyber security, open system architecture (OSA), novel avionics and sensor technologies, and multi-domain technologies. Federal is currently fulfilling the Department of the Air Force, Air Force Material Command (AFMC), Electronic System Center (ESC), 554 ELSG/PK, Wright-Patterson Air Force Base, requirement for Subject Matter Expert (SME) support for the Air Force Equipment Management System (AFEMS) and Stock Control System (SCS). </p>\r\n<p><strong>BACKGROUND:</strong></p>\r\n<p>AFEMS <br />\r\n<br />\r\nThe Air Force Equipment Management System (AFEMS) is designed to provide the United States Air Force with a worldwide accessible, dedicated, totally integrated, transaction-driven, processing system that enables accountability and management of approximately $38B worth of equipment resources. AFEMS is used by Air Force (AF) Equipment Managers world-wide to determine, authorize, account for, provide visibility to, and report the types and quantities of equipment required to accomplish the AF mission, and serves as a primary basis for organizational budget/buy programs. AFEMS processes all AF data for management of equipment, information technology and wireless assets, Special Tooling/Special Test Equipment (ST/STE), and Internal Use Software (IUS) via online web enabled interactive processes. AFEMS provides the AF a centralized equipment requirements system utilized to identify, prioritize and fund equipment buys and formulate equipment budgets. AFEMS is Chief Financial Officer (CFO) compliant and enables capitalization of equipment, Information Technology (IT), ST/STE assets, and IUS meeting the capital threshold to ensure the Plant, Property &amp; Equipment (PP&amp;E) portion of the AF Financial Statement is auditable. AFEMS consists of the following subsystems; Support Equipment (SE) unclassified, SE classified, Asset Information Management (AIM), Equipment Management System (ERS), electronic Access Request Management System (eARMS), and Capital Reporting for CFO requirements. <br />\r\n<br />\r\nFrom a topology standpoint AFEMS runs on two mainframes (unclassified and classified) and sixty plus servers. AFEMS has been partially migrated from the mainframe environment to an n-tier architecture which emulates the GCSS-AF Integration Framework (IF). It is hosted at Wright Patterson AFB on the Air Force network. Operations, maintenance and sustainment support is provided by the sustainment contractor and the Program Management Office (PMO). <br />\r\n<br />\r\nThough AFEMS first went into production as a mainframe application in 1996, it has in the last few years undergone changes to make it web accessible. In FY02 upgrade efforts began to migrate AFEMS functionality to support Global Combat Support System (GCSS) AF Integration Framework (IF) architecture. This involved the use of a spiral development methodology in conjunction with the Rational Unified Process (RUP) to transition legacy code to a GCSS-AF compatible componentized system residing on an n-tier based architecture. This configuration was to provide the means to meet the GCSS-AF mandate for seamlessly integrating all combat support automated information systems into an information-on-demand web-based architecture. Business components were identified, and were in various stages of technology refresh when the December 2003 decision was made to stop technical refresh efforts in AFEMS and redirect enhancement and &ldquo;discretionary&rdquo; sustainment funding to the Expeditionary Combat Support System (ECSS) program. <br />\r\n<br />\r\nThe functional operation of AFEMS is governed by Department of Defense Instruction (DoDI) 5000.64 - Accountability and Management of DoD-Owned Equipment and Other Accountable Property; DFAS 7900.4.G - A Guide to Federal Requirements for Financial Management Systems (Chapters 3 &amp; 14); DoD Financial Management Regulation (Vol 4, Chap. 6); Air Force Manual (AFMAN) 23-110, Volume Two, Part 2, various chapters; AFMCMAN 23-4 Computation of Requirements for Equipment Items, in addition to other guidance. <br />\r\n<br />\r\nSCS <br />\r\n<br />\r\nSCS is a web-based mainframe wholesale and depot retail asset management system used worldwide by the United States Air Force and United States Marine Corps (USMC). It provides enhanced processing of stock control transactions and management information for Air Force and USMC operations. The system directly supports HQ AFMC, the Air Logistics Centers (ALCs), Cryptologic Systems Group (CPSG), USMC, and other Services/Agencies and foreign military sales customers. SCS is a combination of web-based and legacy mainframe architectures, which provides worldwide asset visibility, real-time requisition processing, management control activity for contractor requisitions, and depot supply management. It provides worldwide combat readiness and sustainability for the war fighter through allocation, custody, and distribution of Air Force and USMC managed supply and equipment items. <br />\r\n<br />\r\n<br />\r\nSCS consists of the following modules/functionalities: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Item Manager Wholesale Requisition Process (IMWRP) </li>\r\n    <li>Wholesale Management and Efficiency Report (WMER) </li>\r\n    <li>Reportable Asset Management Process (RAMP) </li>\r\n    <li>Special Support Stock Control (SSSC) </li>\r\n    <li>Readiness Based Leveling (RBL) </li>\r\n    <li>Reutilization and Disposition System (RDS) </li>\r\n    <li>Wholesale and Retail Receiving and Shipping (WARRS) </li>\r\n    <li>Inventory and Storage Process (INSTOR) </li>\r\n    <li>Shipping Information System (SIS) </li>\r\n    <li>Marine Corps Interface Process (MCIP) </li>\r\n    <li>SCS Web Inquiry </li>\r\n    <li>SCS Web Requisitioning </li>\r\n    <li>Financial Inventory and Accounting Billing System (FIABS) </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>SCS is in sustainment status and will be replaced by the Expeditionary Combat Support System (ECSS). <br />\r\n<br />\r\nAFMAN 23-110, USAF Supply Manual, is one of the documents that govern the processes of SCS. </p>\r\n<p><strong>REQUIREMENTS:</strong></p>\r\n<p>HQ 754th ELSG/ILSA requires functional and technical SMEs for AFEMS, SCS, and ECSS as it relates to these two systems. SMEs are individuals with a specific level of expertise in certain key system areas or disciplines and are knowledgeable about the domain being represented. This professional provides unique and/or in-depth functional and technical knowledge on the application and system operations. </p>\r\n<p>The scope of the requirement includes: </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Translate user requirements into system specifications, data management plans, configuration management plans, life cycle management documentation, integrated logistics support plans and related operational summaries </li>\r\n    <li>Gather information from users, define work problems, and design systems and procedures to resolve problems </li>\r\n    <li>Assist in the design, development, and analysis, test and maintenance of logical and physical databases in order to meet functional requirements. Write specification manuals and user documentation for client or user personnel </li>\r\n    <li>Direct enterprise wide strategic systems planning, business information planning, business and analysis </li>\r\n    <li>Manage functional, process, and data modeling in support of the planning and analysis efforts </li>\r\n    <li>Examine and analyze current and contemplated operations for developing, defining, and coordinating user requirements which will satisfy the total program need </li>\r\n    <li>Review data design, proposed system revisions, and test results to ensure functional requirements are met to include batch processes </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>AFEMS requirements encompass:</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Functional Expertise:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Understanding all functional aspects of AFEMS, to include processes and data. Satisfy all functional, security, and configuration management requirements of eARMS </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Computer Based Training:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Manage the AFEMS computer based training modules, which requires personnel with knowledge of and ability to work with Lectora Publisher </li>\r\n    </ul>\r\n    </li>\r\n    <li>Prepare Rough Orders of Magnitude (ROMs) and Technical Solutions (TS) at the SME level of expertise, to include the labor categories required and the estimated number of hours needed and an explanation of the requirement and probable solution </li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>SCS requirements encompass the following (Note: support for FIABS, a module of SCS, is required only for the tasks specified in the paragraphs below): </p>\r\n<ul>\r\n    <li>Functional Expertise:\r\n    <ul>\r\n        <li>Provide functional expertise of the Stock Control processes.
